<tr>\n        <td style="padding:0 0.1em 0.4em">\n         <ul>\n          <li>\n           <a href="/wiki/Arctic_Ocean" title="Arctic Ocean">\n            Arctic\n           </a>\n          </li>\n <hr/>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%">\n         <div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini">\n          <ul>\n           <li </a>\n           </li>\n           <li class="nv-talk">\n            <a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Five_oceans" title="Template talk:Five oceans">\n             <abbr title="Discuss this template">\n              t\n             </abbr>\n            </a>\n           </li>\n           <li class="nv-edit">\n            <a class="external text" </li>\n          </ul>\n         </div>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <b>\n        Pacific Ocean\n       </b>\n       is the largest and deepest of\n       <a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">\n        Earth\n       </a>\n       \'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Ocean" title="Ocean">\n        oceanic\n       </a>\n       divisions. It extends from the\n       <a href="/wiki/Arctic_Ocean" title="Arctic Ocean">\n        Arctic Ocean\n       </a>\n       in the north to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Southern_Ocean" title="Southern Ocean">\n        Southern Ocean\n       </a>\n       (or, depending on definition, to\n       <a href="/wiki/Antarctica" title="Antarctica">\n        Antarctica\n       </a>\n       ) in the south and is bounded by\n       <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">\n        Asia\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Australia_(continent)" title="Australia (continent)">\n        Australia\n       </a>\n       in the west and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">\n        Americas\n       </a>\n       in the east.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       At 165,250,000 square kilometers (63,800,000 square miles) in area (as defined with an Antarctic southern border), this largest division of the\n       <a href="/wiki/World_Ocean" title="World Ocean">\n        World Ocean\n       </a>\n       \xe2\x80\x94and, in turn, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Hydrosphere" title="Hydrosphere">\n        hydrosphere\n       </a>\n       \xe2\x80\x94covers about 46% of Earth\'s water surface and about one-third of its total surface area, making it larger than all of Earth\'s land area combined.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ebc_1-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ebc-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Both the center of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Land_and_water_hemispheres" title="Land and water hemispheres">\n        Water Hemisphere\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Western_Hemisphere" title="Western Hemisphere">\n        Western Hemisphere\n       </a>\n       are in the Pacific Ocean. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Equator" title="Equator">\n        equator\n       </a>\n       subdivides it into the\n       <b>\n        North Pacific Ocean\n       </b>\n       and\n       <b>\n        South Pacific Ocean\n       </b>\n       , with two exceptions: the\n       <a href="/wiki/Gal%C3%A1pagos_Islands" title="Gal\xc3\xa1pagos Islands">\n        Gal\xc3\xa1pagos\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Gilbert_Islands" title="Gilbert Islands">\n        Gilbert Islands\n       </a>\n       , while straddling the equator, are deemed wholly within the South Pacific.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IHO1953_2-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-IHO1953-2">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Its mean depth is 4,280 meters (14,040 feet). The\n       <a href="/wiki/Mariana_Trench" title="Mariana Trench">\n        Mariana Trench\n       </a>\n       in the western North Pacific is the deepest point in the world, reaching a depth of 10,911 meters (35,797 feet).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The western Pacific has many peripheral\n       <a href="/wiki/Sea" title="Sea">\n        seas\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Though the peoples of Asia and Oceania have traveled the Pacific Ocean since prehistoric times, the eastern Pacific was first sighted by Europeans in the early 16th century when Spanish explorer\n       <a href="/wiki/Vasco_N%C3%BA%C3%B1ez_de_Balboa" title="Vasco N\xc3\xba\xc3\xb1ez de Balboa">\n        Vasco N\xc3\xba\xc3\xb1ez de Balboa\n       </a>\n       crossed the\n       <a href="/wiki/Isthmus_of_Panama" title="Isthmus of Panama">\n        Isthmus of Panama\n       </a>\n       in 1513 and discovered the great "southern sea" which he named\n       <i>\n        Mar del Sur\n       </i>\n       (in Spanish). The ocean\'s current name was coined by\n       <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">\n        Portuguese\n       </a>\n       explorer\n       <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_Magellan" title="Ferdinand Magellan">\n        Ferdinand Magellan\n       </a>\n       during the Spanish\n       <a href="/wiki/Circumnavigation" title="Circumnavigation">\n        circumnavigation\n       </a>\n       of the world in 1521, as he encountered favorable winds on reaching the ocean. He called it\n       <i>\n        Mar Pac\xc3\xadfico\n       </i>\n       , which in both\n       <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">\n        Portuguese\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">\n        Spanish\n       </a>\n       means "peaceful sea".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-4">\n         [4]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <div class="toc" id="toc">\n       <div class="toctitle">\n        <h2>\n         Contents\n        </h2>\n       </div>\n       <ul>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1">\n         <a href="#History">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           1\n          </span>\n          <span     European exploration\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-4">\n           <a href="#New_Imperialism">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             1.3\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             New Imperialism\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-5">\n         <a href="#Geography">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           2\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Geography\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-6">\n           <a href="#Bordering_countries_and_territories">\n            <span            <li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-7">\n             <a href="#Sovereign_nations">\n              <span class="tocnumber">\n               2.1.1\n              </span>\n              <span         </a>\n            </li>\n           </ul>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-9">\n           <a href="#Landmasses_and_islands">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             2.2\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Landmasses and islands\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-10">\n         <a href="#Water_characteristics">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           3\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Water characteristics\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-11">\n         <a href="#Climate">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           4\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Climate\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-12">\n         <a href="#Geology">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           5\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Geology\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-13">\n           <a href="#Geological_history">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             5.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Geological history\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-14">\n           <a href="#Seamount_chains">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             5.2\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Seamount chains\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-15">\n         <a href="#Economy">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           6\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Economy\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-16">\n           <a href="#Fishing">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             6.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Fishing\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-17">\n         <a href="#Environmental_issues">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           7\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Environmental issues\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-18">\n         <a href="#Major_ports_and_harbors">\n          <span class="toclevel-1 tocsection-19">\n         <a href="#See_also">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           9\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           See also\n <p>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">\n        History\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Pacific_Ocean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Early_migrations">\n        Early migrations\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Pacific_Ocean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early migrations">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation">\n       <tr>\n        <td class="mbox-image">\n         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg">\n          <img alt="[icon]" data-file-height="31" data-file-width="44" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" width="20"/>\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td class="mbox-text">\n         <div class="mbox-text-span">\n          <b>\n           This section needs expansion\n          </b>\n          .\n          <small>\n           You can help by\n           <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Pacific_Ocean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">\n            adding to it\n           </a>\n           .\n          </small>\n          <small>\n           <i>\n            (October 2017)\n           </i>\n          </small>\n         </div>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Waldseemuller_map_2.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="7590" data-file-width="13708" height="122" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Waldseemuller_map_2.jpg/220px-Waldseemuller_map_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Waldseemuller_map_2.jpg/330px-Waldseemuller_map_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Waldseemuller_map_2.jpg/440px-Waldseemuller_map_2.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Waldseemuller_map_2.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <i>\n          Universalis Cosmographia\n         </i>\n         , the\n         <a href="/wiki/Waldseem%C3%BCller_map" title="Waldseem\xc3\xbcller map">\n          Waldseem\xc3\xbcller map\n         </a>\n         dated 1507, from a time when the nature of the Americas was ambiguous, particularly North America, as a possible part of Asia, was the first map to show the Americas separating two distinct oceans. South America was generally considered a "new world" and shows the name "America" for the first time, after\n         <a href="/wiki/Amerigo_Vespucci" title="Amerigo Vespucci">\n          Amerigo Vespucci\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Carta_universal_en_que_se_contiene_todo_lo_que_del_mundo_se_ha_descubierto_fasta_agora_hizola_Diego_Ribero_cosmographo_de_su_magestad,_ano_de_1529,_en_Sevilla.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2324" data-file-width="5471" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Carta_universal_en_que_se_contiene_todo_lo_que_del_mundo_se_ha_descubierto_fasta_agora_hizola_Diego_Ribero_cosmographo_de_su_magestad%2C_ano_de_1529%2C_en_Sevilla.jpg/220px-thumbnail.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Carta_universal_en_que_se_contiene_todo_lo_que_del_mundo_se_ha_descubierto_fasta_agora_hizola_Diego_Ribero_cosmographo_de_su_magestad%2C_ano_de_1529%2C_en_Sevilla.jpg/330px-thumbnail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Carta_universal_en_que_se_contiene_todo_lo_que_del_mundo_se_ha_descubierto_fasta_agora_hizola_Diego_Ribero_cosmographo_de_su_magestad%2C_ano_de_1529%2C_en_Sevilla.jpg/440px-thumbnail.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Carta_universal_en_que_se_contiene_todo_lo_que_del_mundo_se_ha_descubierto_fasta_agora_hizola_Diego_Ribero_cosmographo_de_su_magestad,_ano_de_1529,_en_Sevilla.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Made in 1529, the\n         <a href="/wiki/Diogo_Ribeiro" title="Diogo Ribeiro">\n          Diogo Ribeiro\n         </a>\n         map was the first to show the Pacific at about its proper size\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ortelius_-_Maris_Pacifici_1589.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2771" data-file-width="4001" height="152" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Ortelius_-_Maris_Pacifici_1589.jpg/220px-Ortelius_-_Maris_Pacifici_1589.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Ortelius_-_Maris_Pacifici_1589.jpg/330px-Ortelius_-_Maris_Pacifici_1589.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Ortelius_-_Maris_Pacifici_1589.jpg/440px-Ortelius_-_Maris_Pacifici_1589.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ortelius_-_Maris_Pacifici_1589.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Maris_Pacifici" title="Maris Pacifici">\n          Maris Pacifici\n         </a>\n         by\n         <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Ortelius" title="Abraham Ortelius">\n          Ortelius\n         </a>\n         (1589). One of the first printed maps to show the Pacific Ocean\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">\n          <a href="#cite_note-5">\n           [5]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Important human migrations occurred in the Pacific in prehistoric times. About 3000\xc2\xa0BC, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Austronesian_peoples" title="Austronesian peoples">\n        Austronesian peoples\n       </a>\n       on the island of\n       <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">\n        Taiwan\n       </a>\n       mastered the art of long-distance canoe travel and spread themselves and their languages south to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">\n        Philippines\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">\n        Indonesia\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Maritime_Southeast_Asia" title="Maritime Southeast Asia">\n        maritime Southeast Asia\n       </a>\n       ; west towards\n       <a href="/wiki/Madagascar" title="Madagascar">\n        Madagascar\n       </a>\n       ; southeast towards\n       <a href="/wiki/New_Guinea" title="New Guinea">\n        New Guinea\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Melanesia" title="Melanesia">\n        Melanesia\n       </a>\n       (intermarrying with native\n       <a href="/wiki/Papuan_people" title="Papuan people">\n        Papuans\n       </a>\n       ); and east to the islands of\n       <a href="/wiki/Micronesia" title="Micronesia">\n        Micronesia\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Oceania" title="Oceania">\n        Oceania\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Polynesia" title="Polynesia">\n        Polynesia\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stanley2004_6-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Stanley2004-6">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Long-distance trade developed all along the coast from\n       <a href="/wiki/Mozambique" title="Mozambique">\n        Mozambique\n       </a>\n       to\n       <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">\n        Japan\n       </a>\n       . Trade, and therefore knowledge, extended to the Indonesian islands but apparently not Australia. By at least 878 when there was a significant Islamic settlement in\n       <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou" title="Guangzhou">\n        Canton\n       </a>\n       much of this trade was controlled by Arabs or Muslims. In 219\xc2\xa0BC\n       <a href="/wiki/Xu_Fu" title="Xu Fu">\n        Xu Fu\n       </a>\n       sailed out into the Pacific searching for the elixir of immortality. From 1404 to 1433\n       <a href="/wiki/Zheng_He" title="Zheng He">\n        Zheng He\n       </a>\n       led\n       <a href="/wiki/Treasure_voyages" title="Treasure voyages">\n        expeditions into the Indian Ocean\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="European_exploration">\n        European exploration\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Pacific_Ocean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: European exploration">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:A_generall_chart_of_the_South_Sea_..._NYPL481132.tiff">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="5428" data-file-width="7230" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/A_generall_chart_of_the_South_Sea_..._NYPL481132.tiff/lossy-page1-220px-A_generall_chart_of_the_South_Sea_..._NYPL481132.tiff.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/A_generall_chart_of_the_South_Sea_..._NYPL481132.tiff/lossy-page1-330px-A_generall_chart_of_the_South_Sea_..._NYPL481132.tiff.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/A_generall_chart_of_the_South_Sea_..._NYPL481132.tiff/lossy-page1-440px-A_generall_chart_of_the_South_Sea_..._NYPL481132.tiff.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:A_generall_chart_of_the_South_Sea_..._NYPL481132.tiff" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Map of the Pacific Ocean during European Exploration, circa 1702\xe2\x80\x931707.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:A_compleat_chart_of_the_coast_of_Asia_and_America_with_the_great_South_Sea_-_R.W._Seale_del._et_sculp._NYPL465242.tiff">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4520" data-file-width="5779" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/A_compleat_chart_of_the_coast_of_Asia_and_America_with_the_great_South_Sea_-_R.W._Seale_del._et_sculp._NYPL465242.tiff/lossy-page1-220px-A_compleat_chart_of_the_coast_of_Asia_and_America_with_the_great_South_Sea_-_R.W._Seale_del._et_sculp._NYPL465242.tiff.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/A_compleat_chart_of_the_coast_of_Asia_and_America_with_the_great_South_Sea_-_R.W._Seale_del._et_sculp._NYPL465242.tiff/lossy-page1-330px-A_compleat_chart_of_the_coast_of_Asia_and_America_with_the_great_South_Sea_-_R.W._Seale_del._et_sculp._NYPL465242.tiff.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/A_compleat_chart_of_the_coast_of_Asia_and_America_with_the_great_South_Sea_-_R.W._Seale_del._et_sculp._NYPL465242.tiff/lossy-page1-440px-A_compleat_chart_of_the_coast_of_Asia_and_America_with_the_great_South_Sea_-_R.W._Seale_del._et_sculp._NYPL465242.tiff.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:A_compleat_chart_of_the_coast_of_Asia_and_America_with_the_great_South_Sea_-_R.W._Seale_del._et_sculp._NYPL465242.tiff" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Map of the Pacific Ocean during European Exploration, circa 1754.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The first contact of European navigators with the western edge of the Pacific Ocean was made by the Portuguese expeditions of\n       <a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3nio_de_Abreu" title="Ant\xc3\xb3nio de Abreu">\n        Ant\xc3\xb3nio de Abreu\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Serr%C3%A3o" title="Francisco Serr\xc3\xa3o">\n        Francisco Serr\xc3\xa3o\n       </a>\n       , via the\n       <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Sunda_Islands" title="Lesser Sunda Islands">\n        Lesser Sunda Islands\n       </a>\n       , to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Maluku_Islands" title="Maluku Islands">\n        Maluku Islands\n       </a>\n       , in 1512,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">\n        <a href="#cite_note-7">\n         [7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">\n        <a href="#cite_note-8">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and with\n       <a href="/wiki/Jorge_%C3%81lvares" title="Jorge \xc3\x81lvares">\n        Jorge \xc3\x81lvares\n       </a>\n       \'s expedition to southern China in 1513,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Porter.2C_Jonathan_1996_9-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Porter.2C_Jonathan_1996-9">\n         [9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       both ordered by\n       <a href="/wiki/Afonso_de_Albuquerque" title="Afonso de Albuquerque">\n        Afonso de Albuquerque\n       </a>\n       from\n       <a href="/wiki/Malacca" title="Malacca">\n        Malacca\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The east side of the ocean was discovered by Spanish explorer\n       <a href="/wiki/Vasco_N%C3%BA%C3%B1ez_de_Balboa" title="Vasco N\xc3\xba\xc3\xb1ez de Balboa">\n        Vasco N\xc3\xba\xc3\xb1ez de Balboa\n       </a>\n       in 1513 after his expedition crossed the\n       <a href="/wiki/Isthmus_of_Panama" title="Isthmus of Panama">\n        Isthmus of Panama\n       </a>\n       and reached a new ocean.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ober_10-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Ober-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       He named it\n       <i>\n        Mar del Sur\n       </i>\n       (literally, "Sea of the South" or "South Sea") because the ocean was to the south of the coast of the isthmus where he first observed the Pacific.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Later, Portuguese explorer\n       <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_Magellan" title="Ferdinand Magellan">\n        Ferdinand Magellan\n       </a>\n       sailed the Pacific East to West on a Castilian (\n       <i>\n        Spanish\n       </i>\n       ) expedition of world\n       <a href="/wiki/Circumnavigation" title="Circumnavigation">\n        circumnavigation\n       </a>\n       starting in 1519. Magellan called the ocean\n       <i>\n        Pac\xc3\xadfico\n       </i>\n       (or "Pacific" meaning, "peaceful") because, after sailing through the stormy seas off\n       <a href="/wiki/Cape_Horn" title="Cape Horn">\n        Cape Horn\n       </a>\n       , the expedition found calm waters. The ocean was often called the\n       <i>\n        Sea of Magellan\n       </i>\n       in his honor until the eighteenth century.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">\n        <a href="#cite_note-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Although Magellan himself died in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">\n        Philippines\n       </a>\n       in 1521, Spanish Basque navigator\n       <a href="/wiki/Juan_Sebasti%C3%A1n_Elcano" title="Juan Sebasti\xc3\xa1n Elcano">\n        Juan Sebasti\xc3\xa1n Elcano\n       </a>\n       led the expedition back to Spain across the\n       <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean" title="Indian Ocean">\n        Indian Ocean\n       </a>\n       and round the\n       <a href="/wiki/Cape_of_Good_Hope" title="Cape of Good Hope">\n        Cape of Good Hope\n       </a>\n       , completing the first world circumnavigation in a single expedition in 1522.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oceanario_12-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-oceanario-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Sailing around and east of the Moluccas, between 1525 and 1527, Portuguese expeditions discovered the\n       <a href="/wiki/Caroline_Islands" title="Caroline Islands">\n        Caroline Islands\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">\n        <a href="#cite_note-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       the\n       <a href="/wiki/Aru_Islands" title="Aru Islands">\n        Aru Islands\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">\n        <a href="#cite_note-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea" title="Papua New Guinea">\n        Papua New Guinea\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Whiteway_15-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Whiteway-15">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In 1542\xe2\x80\x9343 the Portuguese also reached\n       <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">\n        Japan\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">\n        <a href="#cite_note-16">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 1564, five Spanish ships consisting of 379 explorers crossed the ocean from Mexico led by\n       <a href="/wiki/Miguel_L%C3%B3pez_de_Legazpi" title="Miguel L\xc3\xb3pez de Legazpi">\n        Miguel L\xc3\xb3pez de Legazpi\n       </a>\n       and sailed to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">\n        Philippines\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Mariana_Islands" title="Mariana Islands">\n        Mariana Islands\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HendersonDelpar2000_17-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-HendersonDelpar2000-17">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       For the remainder of the 16th century, Spanish influence was paramount, with ships sailing from\n       <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">\n        Mexico\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">\n        Peru\n       </a>\n       across the Pacific Ocean to the Philippines, via\n       <a href="/wiki/Guam" title="Guam">\n        Guam\n       </a>\n       , and establishing the\n       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_East_Indies" title="Spanish East Indies">\n        Spanish East Indies\n       </a>\n       . The\n       <a href="/wiki/Manila_galleon" title="Manila galleon">\n        Manila galleons\n       </a>\n       operated for two and a half centuries linking\n       <a href="/wiki/Manila" title="Manila">\n        Manila\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Acapulco" title="Acapulco">\n        Acapulco\n       </a>\n       , in one of the longest trade routes in history. Spanish expeditions also discovered\n       <a href="/wiki/Tuvalu" title="Tuvalu">\n        Tuvalu\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/Marquesas_Islands" title="Marquesas Islands">\n        Marquesas\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/Cook_Islands" title="Cook Islands">\n        Cook Islands\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Islands" title="Solomon Islands">\n        Solomon Islands\n       </a>\n       , and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Admiralty_Islands" title="Admiralty Islands">\n        Admiralty Islands\n       </a>\n       in the South Pacific.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fernandez-Armesto_2006_305.E2.80.93307_18-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Fernandez-Armesto_2006_305.E2.80.93307-18">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Later, in the quest for\n       <a href="/wiki/Terra_Australis" title="Terra Australis">\n        Terra Australis\n       </a>\n       (i.e., "the [great] Southern Land"), Spanish explorations in the 17th century, such as the expedition led by the Portuguese navigator\n       <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Fernandes_de_Queir%C3%B3s" title="Pedro Fernandes de Queir\xc3\xb3s">\n        Pedro Fernandes de Queir\xc3\xb3s\n       </a>\n       , discovered the\n       <a href="/wiki/Pitcairn_Islands" title="Pitcairn Islands">\n        Pitcairn\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Vanuatu" title="Vanuatu">\n        Vanuatu\n       </a>\n       archipelagos, and sailed the\n       <a href="/wiki/Torres_Strait" title="Torres Strait">\n        Torres Strait\n       </a>\n       between\n       <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">\n        Australia\n       </a>\n       and New Guinea, named after navigator\n       <a href="/wiki/Lu%C3%ADs_Vaz_de_Torres" title="Lu\xc3\xads Vaz de Torres">\n        Lu\xc3\xads Vaz de Torres\n       </a>\n       . Dutch explorers, sailing around southern Africa, also engaged in discovery and trade;\n       <a href="/wiki/Willem_Janszoon" title="Willem Janszoon">\n        Willem Janszoon\n       </a>\n       , made the first completely documented European landing in Australia (1606), in\n       <a href="/wiki/Cape_York_Peninsula" title="Cape York Peninsula">\n        Cape York Peninsula\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">\n        <a href="#cite_note-19">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Abel_Tasman" title="Abel Tasman">\n        Abel Janszoon Tasman\n       </a>\n       circumnavigated and landed on parts of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">\n        Australian\n       </a>\n       continental coast and discovered\n       <a href="/wiki/Tasmania" title="Tasmania">\n        Tasmania\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">\n        New Zealand\n       </a>\n       in 1642.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">\n        <a href="#cite_note-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In the 16th and 17th century Spain considered the Pacific Ocean a\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Mare_clausum" title="Mare clausum">\n         Mare clausum\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       \xe2\x80\x94a sea closed to other naval powers. As the only known entrance from the Atlantic the\n       <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Magellan" title="Strait of Magellan">\n        Strait of Magellan\n       </a>\n       was at times patrolled by fleets sent to prevent entrance of non-Spanish ships. On the western end of the Pacific Ocean the Dutch threatened the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Philippines" title="The Philippines">\n        Spanish Philippines\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lytle_21-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-lytle-21">\n         [21]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The 18th century marked the beginning of major exploration by the Russians in\n       <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">\n        Alaska\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Aleutian_Islands" title="Aleutian Islands">\n        Aleutian Islands\n       </a>\n       , such as the\n       <a href="/wiki/First_Kamchatka_expedition" title="First Kamchatka expedition">\n        First Kamchatka expedition\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Great_Northern_Expedition" title="Great Northern Expedition">\n        Great Northern Expedition\n       </a>\n       , led by the Danish Russian navy officer\n       <a href="/wiki/Vitus_Bering" title="Vitus Bering">\n        Vitus Bering\n       </a>\n       . Spain also sent\n       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_expeditions_to_the_Pacific_Northwest" title="Spanish expeditions to the Pacific Northwest">\n        expeditions to the Pacific Northwest\n       </a>\n       reaching\n       <a href="/wiki/Vancouver_Island" title="Vancouver Island">\n        Vancouver Island\n       </a>\n       in southern Canada, and Alaska. The French explored and settled\n       <a href="/wiki/Polynesia" title="Polynesia">\n        Polynesia\n       </a>\n       , and the British made three voyages with\n       <a href="/wiki/James_Cook" title="James Cook">\n        James Cook\n       </a>\n       to the South Pacific and\n       <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">\n        Australia\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">\n        Hawaii\n       </a>\n       , and the North American\n       <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Northwest" title="Pacific Northwest">\n        Pacific Northwest\n       </a>\n       . In 1768,\n       <a href="/wiki/Pierre-Antoine_V%C3%A9ron" title="Pierre-Antoine V\xc3\xa9ron">\n        Pierre-Antoine V\xc3\xa9ron\n       </a>\n       , a young\n       <a href="/wiki/Astronomer" title="Astronomer">\n        astronomer\n       </a>\n       accompanying\n       <a href="/wiki/Louis_Antoine_de_Bougainville" title="Louis Antoine de Bougainville">\n        Louis Antoine de Bougainville\n       </a>\n       on his voyage of exploration, established the width of the Pacific with precision for the first time in history.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Williams2004_22-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Williams2004-22">\n         [22]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       One of the earliest voyages of scientific exploration was organized by Spain in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Malaspina_Expedition" title="Malaspina Expedition">\n        Malaspina Expedition\n       </a>\n       of 1789\xe2\x80\x931794. It sailed vast areas of the Pacific, from Cape Horn to Alaska, Guam and the Philippines, New Zealand, Australia, and the South Pacific.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fernandez-Armesto_2006_305.E2.80.93307_18-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Fernandez-Armesto_2006_305.E2.80.93307-18">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="New_Imperialism">\n        New Imperialism\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Pacific_Ocean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: New Imperialism">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/New_Imperialism" title="New Imperialism">\n        New Imperialism\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Trieste_(23_Jan_1960).jpeg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="564" data-file-width="723" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Trieste_%2823_Jan_1960%29.jpeg/220px-Trieste_%2823_Jan_1960%29.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Trieste_%2823_Jan_1960%29.jpeg/330px-Trieste_%2823_Jan_1960%29.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Trieste_%2823_Jan_1960%29.jpeg/440px-Trieste_%2823_Jan_1960%29.jpeg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Trieste_(23_Jan_1960).jpeg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The\n         <a href="/wiki/Bathyscaphe_Trieste" title="Bathyscaphe Trieste">\n          Bathyscaphe Trieste\n         </a>\n         , before her record dive to the bottom of the\n         <a href="/wiki/Mariana_Trench" title="Mariana Trench">\n          Mariana Trench\n         </a>\n         , 23 January 1960\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Growing\n       <a href="/wiki/Imperialism" title="Imperialism">\n        imperialism\n       </a>\n       during the 19th century resulted in the occupation of much of Oceania by other European powers, and later,\n       <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">\n        Japan\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">\n        United States\n       </a>\n       . Significant contributions to oceanographic knowledge were made by the voyages of\n       <a href="/wiki/HMS_Beagle" title="HMS Beagle">\n        HMS\n        <i>\n         Beagle\n        </i>\n       </a>\n       in the 1830s, with\n       <a href="/wiki/Charles_Darwin" title="Charles Darwin">\n        Charles Darwin\n       </a>\n       aboard;\n       <a href="/wiki/HMS_Challenger_(1858)" title="HMS Challenger (1858)">\n        HMS\n        <i>\n         Challenger\n        </i>\n       </a>\n       during the 1870s; the\n       <a href="/wiki/USS_Tuscarora_(1861)" title="USS Tuscarora (1861)">\n        USS\n        <i>\n         Tuscarora\n        </i>\n       </a>\n       (1873\xe2\x80\x9376); and the German\n       <i>\n        Gazelle\n       </i>\n       (1874\xe2\x80\x9376).\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2014)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TahitiDupetitThouars.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1162" data-file-width="2247" height="114" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/TahitiDupetitThouars.jpg/220px-TahitiDupetitThouars.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/TahitiDupetitThouars.jpg/330px-TahitiDupetitThouars.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/TahitiDupetitThouars.jpg/440px-TahitiDupetitThouars.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:TahitiDupetitThouars.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Abel_Aubert_Dupetit_Thouars" title="Abel Aubert Dupetit Thouars">\n          Dupetit Thouars\n         </a>\n         taking over\n         <a href="/wiki/Tahiti" title="Tahiti">\n          Tahiti\n         </a>\n         on 9 September 1842\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In Oceania, France got a leading position as imperial power after making\n       <a href="/wiki/Tahiti" title="Tahiti">\n        Tahiti\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/New_Caledonia" title="New Caledonia">\n        New Caledonia\n       </a>\n       protectorates in 1842 and 1853 respectively.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Asiapacific_23-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Asiapacific-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       After navy visits to\n       <a href="/wiki/Easter_Island" title="Easter Island">\n        Easter Island\n       </a>\n       in 1875 and 1887, Chilean navy officer\n       <a href="/wiki/Policarpo_Toro" title="Policarpo Toro">\n        Policarpo Toro\n       </a>\n       managed to negotiate an incorporation of the island into Chile with native\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rapanui" title="Rapanui">\n        Rapanui\n       </a>\n       in 1888. By occupying Easter Island, Chile joined the imperial nations.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sater_24-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sater-24">\n         [24]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        (p53)\n       </sup>\n       By 1900 nearly all Pacific islands were in control of Britain, France, United States, Germany, Japan, and Chile.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Asiapacific_23-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Asiapacific-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Although the United States gained control of\n       <a href="/wiki/Guam" title="Guam">\n        Guam\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">\n        Philippines\n       </a>\n       from\n       <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">\n        Spain\n       </a>\n       in 1898,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TewariAlvarez2008_25-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-TewariAlvarez2008-25">\n         [25]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Japan controlled most of the western Pacific by 1914 and occupied many other islands during\n       <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">\n        World War II\n       </a>\n       . However, by the end of that war, Japan was defeated and the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">\n        U.S. Pacific Fleet\n       </a>\n       was the virtual master of the ocean. Since the end of World War II, many former colonies in the Pacific have become independent\n       <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">\n        states\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">\n        Geography\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Pacific_Ocean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Geography">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Iss007e10807.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1853" data-file-width="3032" height="134" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Iss007e10807.jpg/220px-Iss007e10807.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Iss007e10807.jpg/330px-Iss007e10807.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Iss007e10807.jpg/440px-Iss007e10807.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Iss007e10807.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Sunset over the Pacific Ocean as seen from the\n         <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">\n          International Space Station\n         </a>\n         . Anvil tops of\n         <a href="/wiki/Cumulonimbus_cloud" title="Cumulonimbus cloud">\n          thunderclouds\n         </a>\n         are also visible.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The Pacific separates\n       <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">\n        Asia\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">\n        Australia\n       </a>\n       from the\n       <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">\n        Americas\n       </a>\n       . It may be further subdivided by the equator into northern (North Pacific) and southern (South Pacific) portions. It extends from the\n       <a href="/wiki/Antarctic" title="Antarctic">\n        Antarctic\n       </a>\n       region in the South to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Arctic" title="Arctic">\n        Arctic\n       </a>\n       in the north.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ebc_1-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ebc-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The Pacific Ocean encompasses approximately one-third of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">\n        Earth\n       </a>\n       \'s surface, having an area of 165,200,000\xc2\xa0km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       (63,800,000\xc2\xa0sq\xc2\xa0mi)\xe2\x80\x94significantly larger than Earth\'s entire landmass of some 150,000,000\xc2\xa0km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       (58,000,000\xc2\xa0sq\xc2\xa0mi).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">\n        <a href="#cite_note-26">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Extending approximately 15,500\xc2\xa0km (9,600\xc2\xa0mi) from the\n       <a href="/wiki/Bering_Sea" title="Bering Sea">\n        Bering Sea\n       </a>\n       in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Arctic" title="Arctic">\n        Arctic\n       </a>\n       to the northern extent of the circumpolar\n       <a href="/wiki/Southern_Ocean" title="Southern Ocean">\n        Southern Ocean\n       </a>\n       at\n       <a href="/wiki/60th_parallel_south" title="60th parallel south">\n        60\xc2\xb0S\n       </a>\n       (older definitions extend it to\n       <a href="/wiki/Antarctica" title="Antarctica">\n        Antarctica\n       </a>\n       \'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Ross_Sea" title="Ross Sea">\n        Ross Sea\n       </a>\n       ), the Pacific reaches its greatest east-west width at about\n       <a href="/wiki/5th_parallel_north" title="5th parallel north">\n        5\xc2\xb0N latitude\n       </a>\n       , where it stretches approximately 19,800\xc2\xa0km (12,300\xc2\xa0mi) from\n       <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">\n        Indonesia\n       </a>\n       to the coast of\n       <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">\n        Colombia\n       </a>\n       \xe2\x80\x94halfway around the world, and more than five times the diameter of the Moon.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nuttall2005_27-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Nuttall2005-27">\n         [27]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The lowest known point on Earth\xe2\x80\x94the\n       <a href="/wiki/Mariana_Trench" title="Mariana Trench">\n        Mariana Trench\n       </a>\n       \xe2\x80\x94lies 10,911\xc2\xa0m (35,797\n       <a href="/wiki/Foot_(unit)" title="Foot (unit)">\n        ft\n       </a>\n       ; 5,966\n       <a href="/wiki/Fathom" title="Fathom">\n        fathoms\n       </a>\n       ) below sea level. Its average depth is 4,280\xc2\xa0m (14,040\xc2\xa0ft; 2,340 fathoms), putting the total water volume at roughly 710,000,000\xc2\xa0km\n       <sup>\n        3\n       </sup>\n       (170,000,000\xc2\xa0cu\xc2\xa0mi).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ebc_1-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ebc-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Due to the effects of\n       <a href="/wiki/Plate_tectonics" title="Plate tectonics">\n        plate tectonics\n       </a>\n       , the Pacific Ocean is currently shrinking by roughly 2.5\xc2\xa0cm (1\xc2\xa0in) per year on three sides, roughly averaging 0.52\xc2\xa0km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       (0.20\xc2\xa0sq\xc2\xa0mi) a year. By contrast, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">\n        Atlantic Ocean\n       </a>\n       is increasing in size.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">\n        <a href="#cite_note-28">\n         [28]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Young2009_29-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Young2009-29">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Along the Pacific Ocean\'s irregular western margins lie many seas, the largest of which are the\n       <a href="/wiki/Celebes_Sea" title="Celebes Sea">\n        Celebes Sea\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Coral_Sea" title="Coral Sea">\n        Coral Sea\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/East_China_Sea" title="East China Sea">\n        East China Sea\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Sea" title="Philippine Sea">\n        Philippine Sea\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Japan" title="Sea of Japan">\n        Sea of Japan\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/South_China_Sea" title="South China Sea">\n        South China Sea\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Sulu_Sea" title="Sulu Sea">\n        Sulu Sea\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Tasman_Sea" title="Tasman Sea">\n        Tasman Sea\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Yellow_Sea" title="Yellow Sea">\n        Yellow Sea\n       </a>\n       . The\n       <a href="/wiki/Geology_of_Indonesia#Indonesian_Seaway" title="Geology of Indonesia">\n        Indonesian Seaway\n       </a>\n       (including the\n       <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Malacca" title="Strait of Malacca">\n        Strait of Malacca\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Torres_Strait" title="Torres Strait">\n        Torres Strait\n       </a>\n       ) joins the Pacific and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean" title="Indian Ocean">\n        Indian Ocean\n       </a>\n       to the west, and\n       <a href="/wiki/Drake_Passage" title="Drake Passage">\n        Drake Passage\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Magellan" title="Strait of Magellan">\n        Strait of Magellan\n       </a>\n       link the Pacific with the\n       <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">\n        Atlantic Ocean\n       </a>\n       on the east. To the north, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Bering_Strait" title="Bering Strait">\n        Bering Strait\n       </a>\n       connects the Pacific with the\n       <a href="/wiki/Arctic_Ocean" title="Arctic Ocean">\n        Arctic Ocean\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Organization1953_30-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Organization1953-30">\n         [30]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       As the Pacific straddles the\n       <a href="/wiki/180th_meridian" title="180th meridian">\n        180th meridian\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <i>\n        West Pacific\n       </i>\n       (or\n       <i>\n        western Pacific\n       </i>\n       , near Asia) is in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Hemisphere" title="Eastern Hemisphere">\n        Eastern Hemisphere\n       </a>\n       , while the\n       <i>\n        East Pacific\n       </i>\n       (or\n       <i>\n        eastern Pacific\n       </i>\n       , near the Americas) is in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Western_Hemisphere" title="Western Hemisphere">\n        Western Hemisphere\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lydia_31-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Lydia-31">\n         [31]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The Southern Pacific Ocean harbors the\n       <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Indian_Ridge" title="Southeast Indian Ridge">\n        Southeast Indian Ridge\n       </a>\n       crossing from south of\n       <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">\n        Australia\n       </a>\n       turning into the\n       <a href="/wiki/Pacific-Antarctic_Ridge" title="Pacific-Antarctic Ridge">\n        Pacific-Antarctic Ridge\n       </a>\n       (north of the\n       <a href="/wiki/South_Pole" title="South Pole">\n        South Pole\n       </a>\n       ) and merges with another ridge (south of\n       <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">\n        South America\n       </a>\n       ) to form the\n       <a href="/wiki/East_Pacific_Rise" title="East Pacific Rise">\n        East Pacific Rise\n       </a>\n       which also connects with another ridge (south of\n       <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">\n        North America\n       </a>\n       ) which overlooks the\n       <a href="/wiki/Juan_de_Fuca_Ridge" title="Juan de Fuca Ridge">\n        Juan de Fuca Ridge\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       For most of Magellan\'s voyage from the\n       <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Magellan" title="Strait of Magellan">\n        Strait of Magellan\n       </a>\n       to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">\n        Philippines\n       </a>\n       , the explorer indeed found the ocean peaceful. However, the Pacific is not always peaceful. Many\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tropical_storm" title="Tropical storm">\n        tropical storms\n       </a>\n       batter the islands of the Pacific.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">\n        <a href="#cite_note-32">\n         [32]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The lands around the\n       <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Rim" title="Pacific Rim">\n        Pacific Rim\n       </a>\n       are full of\n       <a href="/wiki/Volcano" title="Volcano">\n        volcanoes\n       </a>\n       and often affected by\n       <a href="/wiki/Earthquake" title="Earthquake">\n        earthquakes\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Murphy1979_33-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Murphy1979-33">\n         [33]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Tsunami" title="Tsunami">\n        Tsunamis\n       </a>\n       , caused by underwater earthquakes, have devastated many islands and in some cases destroyed entire towns.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bryant2008_34-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Bryant2008-34">\n         [34]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Martin_Waldseem%C3%BCller" title="Martin Waldseem\xc3\xbcller">\n        Martin Waldseem\xc3\xbcller\n       </a>\n       map of 1507 was the first to show the Americas separating two distinct oceans.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">\n        <a href="#cite_note-35">\n         [35]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Later, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Diogo_Ribeiro" title="Diogo Ribeiro">\n        Diogo Ribeiro\n       </a>\n       map of 1529 was the first to show the Pacific at about its proper size.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">\n        <a href="#cite_note-36">\n         [36]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Bordering_countries_and_territories">\n      </a>\n         (China)\n        </li>\n        <li>\n         <span class="flagicon">\n          <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">\n           <img alt="United States"           <img alt="United States" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="1235" height="12" href="/wiki/Wake_Island" title="Wake Island">\n          Wake Island\n         </a>\n         (US)\n        </li>\n       </ul>\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Landmasses_and_islands">\n        Landmasses and islands\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Pacific_Ocean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Landmasses and islands">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Islands" title="Pacific Islands">\n        Pacific Islands\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       This ocean has most of the islands in the world. There are about 25,000 islands in the Pacific Ocean.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">\n        <a href="#cite_note-37">\n         [37]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">\n        <a href="#cite_note-38">\n         [38]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">\n        <a href="#cite_note-39">\n         [39]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The islands entirely within the Pacific Ocean can be divided into three main groups known as\n       <a href="/wiki/Micronesia" title="Micronesia">\n        Micronesia\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Melanesia" title="Melanesia">\n        Melanesia\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Polynesia" title="Polynesia">\n        Polynesia\n       </a>\n       . Micronesia, which lies north of the equator and west of the\n       <a href="/wiki/International_Date_Line" title="International Date Line">\n        International Date Line\n       </a>\n       , includes the\n       <a href="/wiki/Mariana_Islands" title="Mariana Islands">\n        Mariana Islands\n       </a>\n       in the northwest, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Caroline_Islands" title="Caroline Islands">\n        Caroline Islands\n       </a>\n       in the center, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Islands" title="Marshall Islands">\n        Marshall Islands\n       </a>\n       to the west and the islands of\n       <a href="/wiki/Kiribati" title="Kiribati">\n        Kiribati\n       </a>\n       in the southeast.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AAE_40-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-AAE-40">\n         [40]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LalFortune2000p63_41-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-LalFortune2000p63-41">\n         [41]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Melanesia, to the southwest, includes\n       <a href="/wiki/New_Guinea" title="New Guinea">\n        New Guinea\n       </a>\n       , the world\'s second largest island after\n       <a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">\n        Greenland\n       </a>\n       and by far the largest of the Pacific islands. The other main Melanesian groups from north to south are the\n       <a href="/wiki/Bismarck_Archipelago" title="Bismarck Archipelago">\n        Bismarck Archipelago\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Islands" title="Solomon Islands">\n        Solomon Islands\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_Islands" title="Santa Cruz Islands">\n        Santa Cruz\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Vanuatu" title="Vanuatu">\n        Vanuatu\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Fiji" title="Fiji">\n        Fiji\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/New_Caledonia" title="New Caledonia">\n        New Caledonia\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-West2009_42-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-West2009-42">\n         [42]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The largest area,\n       <a href="/wiki/Polynesia" title="Polynesia">\n        Polynesia\n       </a>\n       , stretching from\n       <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">\n        Hawaii\n       </a>\n       in the north to\n       <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">\n        New Zealand\n       </a>\n       in the south, also encompasses\n       <a href="/wiki/Tuvalu" title="Tuvalu">\n        Tuvalu\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Tokelau" title="Tokelau">\n        Tokelau\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Samoa" title="Samoa">\n        Samoa\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Tonga" title="Tonga">\n        Tonga\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Kermadec_Islands" title="Kermadec Islands">\n        Kermadec Islands\n       </a>\n       to the west, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Cook_Islands" title="Cook Islands">\n        Cook Islands\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Society_Islands" title="Society Islands">\n        Society Islands\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Austral_Islands" title="Austral Islands">\n        Austral Islands\n       </a>\n       in the center, and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Marquesas_Islands" title="Marquesas Islands">\n        Marquesas Islands\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Tuamotus" title="Tuamotus">\n        Tuamotu\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mangareva_Islands" title="Mangareva Islands">\n        Mangareva Islands\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Easter_Island" title="Easter Island">\n        Easter Island\n       </a>\n       to the east.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DunfordRidgell1996_43-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-DunfordRidgell1996-43">\n         [43]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Islands in the Pacific Ocean are of four basic types: continental islands, high islands, coral reefs and uplifted coral platforms. Continental islands lie outside the andesite line and include New Guinea, the islands of New Zealand, and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">\n        Philippines\n       </a>\n       . Some of these islands are structurally associated with nearby continents. High islands are of volcanic origin, and many contain active volcanoes. Among these are\n       <a href="/wiki/Bougainville_Island" title="Bougainville Island">\n        Bougainville\n       </a>\n       , Hawaii, and the Solomon Islands.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GillespieClague2009_44-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-GillespieClague2009-44">\n         [44]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Coral_reef" title="Coral reef">\n        coral reefs\n       </a>\n       of the South Pacific are low-lying structures that have built up on basaltic lava flows under the ocean\'s surface. One of the most dramatic is the\n       <a href="/wiki/Great_Barrier_Reef" title="Great Barrier Reef">\n        Great Barrier Reef\n       </a>\n       off northeastern\n       <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">\n        Australia\n       </a>\n       with chains of reef patches. A second island type formed of coral is the uplifted coral platform, which is usually slightly larger than the low coral islands. Examples include\n       <a href="/wiki/Banaba_Island" title="Banaba Island">\n        Banaba\n       </a>\n       (formerly Ocean Island) and\n       <a href="/wiki/Makatea" title="Makatea">\n        Makatea\n       </a>\n       in the Tuamotu group of\n       <a href="/wiki/French_Polynesia" title="French Polynesia">\n        French Polynesia\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">\n        <a href="#cite_note-45">\n         [45]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">\n        <a href="#cite_note-46">\n         [46]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">\n       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 235px">\n        <div style="width: 235px">\n         <div </p>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n       </li>\n       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 235px">\n        <div style="width: 235px">\n         <div class="thumb" style="width: 230px;">\n          <div style="margin:20px auto;">\n           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Los_Molinos.JPG">\n            <img alt="" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="4000" height="150"
