      <p>\n           <a href="/wiki/Los_Molinos,_Chile" title="Los Molinos, Chile">\n            Los Molinos\n           </a>\n           on the coast of\n           <a href="/wiki/Zona_Sur" title="Zona Sur">\n            Southern Chile\n           </a>\n          </p>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Water_characteristics">\n        Water characteristics\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Pacific_Ocean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Water characteristics">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sunset_Marina.JPG">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Sunset_Marina.JPG/220px-Sunset_Marina.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Sunset_Marina.JPG/330px-Sunset_Marina.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Sunset_Marina.JPG/440px-Sunset_Marina.JPG 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sunset_Marina.JPG" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Sunset in\n         <a href="/wiki/Monterey_County,_California" title="Monterey County, California">\n          Monterey County, California\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">\n          U.S.\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The volume of the Pacific Ocean, representing about 50.1 percent of the world\'s oceanic water, has been estimated at some 714\xc2\xa0million cubic kilometers (171\xc2\xa0million cubic miles).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">\n        <a href="#cite_note-47">\n         [47]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Surface water temperatures in the Pacific can vary from \xe2\x88\x921.4\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C (29.5\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F), the freezing point of sea water, in the poleward areas to about 30\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C (86\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F) near the equator.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mongillo2000_48-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Mongillo2000-48">\n         [48]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Salinity" title="Salinity">\n        Salinity\n       </a>\n       also varies latitudinally, reaching a maximum of 37 parts per thousand in the southeastern area. The water near the equator, which can have a salinity as low as 34 parts per thousand, is less salty than that found in the mid-latitudes because of abundant equatorial precipitation throughout the year. The lowest counts of less than 32 parts per thousand are found in the far north as less evaporation of seawater takes place in these frigid areas.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">\n        <a href="#cite_note-49">\n         [49]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The motion of Pacific waters is generally clockwise in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Northern_Hemisphere" title="Northern Hemisphere">\n        Northern Hemisphere\n       </a>\n       (the\n       <a href="/wiki/Ocean_gyre" title="Ocean gyre">\n        North Pacific gyre\n       </a>\n       ) and counter-clockwise in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Southern_Hemisphere" title="Southern Hemisphere">\n        Southern Hemisphere\n       </a>\n       . The\n       <a href="/wiki/North_Equatorial_Current" title="North Equatorial Current">\n        North Equatorial Current\n       </a>\n       , driven westward along\n       <a href="/wiki/15th_parallel_north" title="15th parallel north">\n        latitude 15\xc2\xb0N\n       </a>\n       by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Trade_winds" title="Trade winds">\n        trade winds\n       </a>\n       , turns north near the\n       <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">\n        Philippines\n       </a>\n       to become the warm Japan or\n       <a href="/wiki/Kuroshio_Current" title="Kuroshio Current">\n        Kuroshio Current\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">\n        <a href="#cite_note-50">\n         [50]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Turning eastward at about\n       <a href="/wiki/45th_parallel_north" title="45th parallel north">\n        45\xc2\xb0N\n       </a>\n       , the Kuroshio forks and some water moves northward as the\n       <a href="/wiki/Aleutian_Current" title="Aleutian Current">\n        Aleutian Current\n       </a>\n       , while the rest turns southward to rejoin the North Equatorial Current.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">\n        <a href="#cite_note-51">\n         [51]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The Aleutian Current branches as it approaches North America and forms the base of a counter-clockwise circulation in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Bering_Sea" title="Bering Sea">\n        Bering Sea\n       </a>\n       . Its southern arm becomes the chilled slow, south-flowing\n       <a href="/wiki/California_Current" title="California Current">\n        California Current\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">\n        <a href="#cite_note-52">\n         [52]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/South_Equatorial_Current" title="South Equatorial Current">\n        South Equatorial Current\n       </a>\n       , flowing west along the equator, swings southward east of\n       <a href="/wiki/New_Guinea" title="New Guinea">\n        New Guinea\n       </a>\n       , turns east at about\n       <a href="/wiki/50th_parallel_south" title="50th parallel south">\n        50\xc2\xb0S\n       </a>\n       , and joins the main westerly circulation of the South Pacific, which includes the Earth-circling\n       <a href="/wiki/Antarctic_Circumpolar_Current" title="Antarctic Circumpolar Current">\n        Antarctic Circumpolar Current\n       </a>\n       . As it approaches the\n       <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">\n        Chilean\n       </a>\n       coast, the South Equatorial Current divides; one branch flows around\n       <a href="/wiki/Cape_Horn" title="Cape Horn">\n        Cape Horn\n       </a>\n       and the other turns north to form the Peru or\n       <a href="/wiki/Humboldt_Current" title="Humboldt Current">\n        Humboldt Current\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">\n        <a href="#cite_note-53">\n         [53]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">\n        Climate\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Pacific_Ocean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Climate">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:El_nino_north_american_weather.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="677" data-file-width="529" height="320" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/El_nino_north_american_weather.png/250px-El_nino_north_american_weather.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/El_nino_north_american_weather.png/375px-El_nino_north_american_weather.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/El_nino_north_american_weather.png/500px-El_nino_north_american_weather.png 2x" width="250"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:El_nino_north_american_weather.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Impact of El Ni\xc3\xb1o and La Ni\xc3\xb1a on North America\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Typhoon_tip_peak.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="560" data-file-width="560" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Typhoon_tip_peak.jpg/220px-Typhoon_tip_peak.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Typhoon_tip_peak.jpg/330px-Typhoon_tip_peak.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Typhoon_tip_peak.jpg/440px-Typhoon_tip_peak.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Typhoon_tip_peak.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Tip" title="Typhoon Tip">\n          Typhoon Tip\n         </a>\n         at global peak intensity on 12 October 1979\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The climate patterns of the Northern and Southern Hemispheres generally mirror each other. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Trade_winds" title="Trade winds">\n        trade winds\n       </a>\n       in the southern and eastern Pacific are remarkably steady while conditions in the North Pacific are far more varied with, for example, cold winter temperatures on the east coast of Russia contrasting with the milder weather off\n       <a href="/wiki/British_Columbia" title="British Columbia">\n        British Columbia\n       </a>\n       during the winter months due to the preferred flow of ocean currents.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">\n        <a href="#cite_note-54">\n         [54]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In the tropical and subtropical Pacific, the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/El_Ni%C3%B1o_Southern_Oscillation" title="El Ni\xc3\xb1o Southern Oscillation">\n        El Ni\xc3\xb1o Southern Oscillation\n       </a>\n       (ENSO) affects weather conditions. To determine the phase of ENSO, the most recent three-month sea surface temperature average for the area approximately 3,000\xc2\xa0km (1,900\xc2\xa0mi) to the southeast of\n       <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">\n        Hawaii\n       </a>\n       is computed, and if the region is more than 0.5\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C (0.9\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F) above or below normal for that period, then an\n       <a href="/wiki/El_Ni%C3%B1o" title="El Ni\xc3\xb1o">\n        El Ni\xc3\xb1o\n       </a>\n       or\n       <a href="/wiki/La_Ni%C3%B1a" title="La Ni\xc3\xb1a">\n        La Ni\xc3\xb1a\n       </a>\n       is considered in progress.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">\n        <a href="#cite_note-55">\n         [55]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In the tropical western Pacific, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Monsoon" title="Monsoon">\n        monsoon\n       </a>\n       and the related\n       <a href="/wiki/Wet_season" title="Wet season">\n        wet season\n       </a>\n       during the summer months contrast with dry winds in the winter which blow over the ocean from the Asian landmass.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">\n        <a href="#cite_note-56">\n         [56]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Worldwide,\n       <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone" title="Tropical cyclone">\n        tropical cyclone\n       </a>\n       activity peaks in late summer, when the difference between temperatures aloft and sea surface temperatures is the greatest. However, each particular basin has its own seasonal patterns. On a worldwide scale, May is the least active month, while September is the most active month. November is the only month in which all the\n       <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_basins" title="Tropical cyclone basins">\n        tropical cyclone basins\n       </a>\n       are active.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AOML_FAQ_G1_57-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-AOML_FAQ_G1-57">\n         [57]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The Pacific hosts the two most active\n       <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_basins" title="Tropical cyclone basins">\n        tropical cyclone basins\n       </a>\n       , which are the northwestern Pacific and the eastern Pacific.\n       <a href="/wiki/Pacific_hurricane" title="Pacific hurricane">\n        Pacific hurricanes\n       </a>\n       form south of\n       <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">\n        Mexico\n       </a>\n       , sometimes striking the western Mexican coast and occasionally the southwestern United States between June and October, while\n       <a href="/wiki/Typhoon" title="Typhoon">\n        typhoons\n       </a>\n       forming in the northwestern Pacific moving into southeast and east Asia from May to December. Tropical cyclones also form in the\n       <a href="/wiki/South_Pacific_tropical_cyclone" title="South Pacific tropical cyclone">\n        South Pacific basin\n       </a>\n       , where they occasionally impact island nations.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In the arctic, icing from October to May can present a hazard for shipping while persistent fog occurs from June to December.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">\n        <a href="#cite_note-58">\n         [58]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A climatological low in the Gulf of Alaska keeps the southern coast wet and mild during the winter months. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Westerlies" title="Westerlies">\n        Westerlies\n       </a>\n       and associated\n       <a href="/wiki/Jet_stream" title="Jet stream">\n        jet stream\n       </a>\n       within the Mid-Latitudes can be particularly strong, especially in the Southern Hemisphere, due to the temperature difference between the tropics and Antarctica,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stimac_59-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Stimac-59">\n         [59]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       which records the coldest temperature readings on the planet. In the Southern hemisphere, because of the stormy and cloudy conditions associated with\n       <a href="/wiki/Extratropical_cyclone" title="Extratropical cyclone">\n        extratropical cyclones\n       </a>\n       riding the jet stream, it is usual to refer to the Westerlies as the Roaring Forties, Furious Fifties and Shrieking Sixties according to the varying degrees of latitude.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">\n        <a href="#cite_note-60">\n         [60]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geology">\n        Geology\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Pacific_Ocean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Geology">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main articles:\n       <a href="/wiki/Geology_of_the_Pacific_Ocean" title="Geology of the Pacific Ocean">\n        Geology of the Pacific Ocean\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Plate" title="Pacific Plate">\n        Pacific Plate\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pacific_Ring_of_Fire.svg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="569" data-file-width="942" height="169" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Pacific_Ring_of_Fire.svg/280px-Pacific_Ring_of_Fire.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Pacific_Ring_of_Fire.svg/420px-Pacific_Ring_of_Fire.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Pacific_Ring_of_Fire.svg/560px-Pacific_Ring_of_Fire.svg.png 2x" width="280"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pacific_Ring_of_Fire.svg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Ring_of_Fire" title="Ring of Fire">\n          Ring of Fire\n         </a>\n         . The Pacific is ringed by many volcanoes and\n         <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_trench" title="Oceanic trench">\n          oceanic trenches\n         </a>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ulawun.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="640" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Ulawun.jpg/220px-Ulawun.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Ulawun.jpg/330px-Ulawun.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Ulawun.jpg/440px-Ulawun.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ulawun.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Ulawun" title="Ulawun">\n          Ulawun\n         </a>\n         stratovolcano situated on the island of\n         <a href="/wiki/New_Britain" title="New Britain">\n          New Britain\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea" title="Papua New Guinea">\n          Papua New Guinea\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The ocean was first mapped by\n       <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Ortelius" title="Abraham Ortelius">\n        Abraham Ortelius\n       </a>\n       ; he called it Maris Pacifici following\n       <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_Magellan" title="Ferdinand Magellan">\n        Ferdinand Magellan\n       </a>\n       \'s description of it as "a pacific sea" during his circumnavigation from 1519 to 1522. To Magellan, it seemed much more calm (pacific) than the Atlantic.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Library2006_61-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Library2006-61">\n         [61]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Andesite_line" title="Andesite line">\n        andesite line\n       </a>\n       is the most significant regional distinction in the Pacific. A petrologic boundary, it separates the deeper,\n       <a href="/wiki/Mafic" title="Mafic">\n        mafic\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Igneous_rock" title="Igneous rock">\n        igneous rock\n       </a>\n       of the Central Pacific Basin from the partially submerged continental areas of\n       <a href="/wiki/Felsic" title="Felsic">\n        felsic\n       </a>\n       igneous rock on its margins.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TrentHazlett2010_62-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-TrentHazlett2010-62">\n         [62]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The andesite line follows the western edge of the islands off\n       <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">\n        California\n       </a>\n       and passes south of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Aleutian_Islands" title="Aleutian Islands">\n        Aleutian arc\n       </a>\n       , along the eastern edge of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Kamchatka_Peninsula" title="Kamchatka Peninsula">\n        Kamchatka Peninsula\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/Kuril_Islands" title="Kuril Islands">\n        Kuril Islands\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">\n        Japan\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/Mariana_Islands" title="Mariana Islands">\n        Mariana Islands\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Islands" title="Solomon Islands">\n        Solomon Islands\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">\n        New Zealand\n       </a>\n       \'s\n       <a href="/wiki/North_Island" title="North Island">\n        North Island\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LalFortune2000p4_63-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-LalFortune2000p4-63">\n         [63]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mueller-Dombois1998_64-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Mueller-Dombois1998-64">\n         [64]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The dissimilarity continues northeastward along the western edge of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Andes" title="Andes">\n        Andes\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/American_Cordillera" title="American Cordillera">\n        Cordillera\n       </a>\n       along\n       <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">\n        South America\n       </a>\n       to\n       <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">\n        Mexico\n       </a>\n       , returning then to the islands off California.\n       <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">\n        Indonesia\n       </a>\n       , the Philippines, Japan, New Guinea, and New Zealand lie outside the andesite line.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Within the closed loop of the andesite line are most of the deep troughs, submerged volcanic mountains, and oceanic volcanic islands that characterize the Pacific basin. Here basaltic lavas gently flow out of rifts to build huge dome-shaped volcanic mountains whose eroded summits form island arcs, chains, and clusters. Outside the andesite line, volcanism is of the explosive type, and the Pacific\n       <a href="/wiki/Ring_of_Fire" title="Ring of Fire">\n        Ring of Fire\n       </a>\n       is the world\'s foremost belt of explosive\n       <a href="/wiki/Volcanism" title="Volcanism">\n        volcanism\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AAE_40-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-AAE-40">\n         [40]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The Ring of Fire is named after the several hundred active volcanoes that sit above the various subduction zones.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The Pacific Ocean is the only ocean which is almost totally bounded by\n       <a href="/wiki/Subduction" title="Subduction">\n        subduction\n       </a>\n       zones. Only the Antarctic and Australian coasts have no nearby subduction zones.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geological_history">\n        Geological history\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Pacific_Ocean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Geological history">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The Pacific Ocean was born 750 million years ago at the breakup of\n       <a href="/wiki/Rodinia" title="Rodinia">\n        Rodinia\n       </a>\n       , although it is generally called the Panthalassic Ocean until the breakup of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pangea" title="Pangea">\n        Pangea\n       </a>\n       , about 200 million years ago.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-geol.umd.edu_65-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-geol.umd.edu-65">\n         [65]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The oldest Pacific Ocean floor is only around 180\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mega-annum" title="Mega-annum">\n        Ma\n       </a>\n       old, with older crust subducted by now.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MussettKhan2000_66-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-MussettKhan2000-66">\n         [66]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Seamount_chains">\n        Seamount chains\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Pacific_Ocean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Seamount chains">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The Pacific Ocean contains several long\n       <a href="/wiki/Seamount" title="Seamount">\n        seamount\n       </a>\n       chains, formed by\n       <a href="/wiki/Hotspot_(geology)" title="Hotspot (geology)">\n        hotspot volcanism\n       </a>\n       . These include the\n       <a href="/wiki/Hawaiian%E2%80%93Emperor_seamount_chain" title="Hawaiian\xe2\x80\x93Emperor seamount chain">\n        Hawaiian\xe2\x80\x93Emperor seamount chain\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Louisville_Ridge" title="Louisville Ridge">\n        Louisville Ridge\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">\n        Economy\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Pacific_Ocean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Economy">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       The exploitation of the Pacific\'s mineral wealth is hampered by the ocean\'s great depths. In shallow waters of the continental shelves off the coasts of Australia and New Zealand,\n       <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">\n        petroleum\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">\n        natural gas\n       </a>\n       are extracted, and\n       <a href="/wiki/Pearl" title="Pearl">\n        pearls\n       </a>\n       are harvested along the coasts of\n       <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">\n        Australia\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">\n        Japan\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea" title="Papua New Guinea">\n        Papua New Guinea\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Nicaragua" title="Nicaragua">\n        Nicaragua\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Panama" title="Panama">\n        Panama\n       </a>\n       , and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">\n        Philippines\n       </a>\n       , although in sharply declining volume in some cases.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">\n        <a href="#cite_note-67">\n         [67]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Fishing">\n        Fishing\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Pacific_Ocean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Fishing">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Fish" title="Fish">\n        Fish\n       </a>\n       are an important economic asset in the Pacific. The shallower shoreline waters of the continents and the more temperate islands yield\n       <a href="/wiki/Herring" title="Herring">\n        herring\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Salmon" title="Salmon">\n        salmon\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Sardine" title="Sardine">\n        sardines\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Australasian_snapper" title="Australasian snapper">\n        snapper\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Swordfish" title="Swordfish">\n        swordfish\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Tuna" title="Tuna">\n        tuna\n       </a>\n       , as well as\n       <a href="/wiki/Shellfish" title="Shellfish">\n        shellfish\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">\n        <a href="#cite_note-68">\n         [68]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Overfishing has become a serious problem in some areas. For example, catches in the rich fishing grounds of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Okhotsk" title="Sea of Okhotsk">\n        Okhotsk Sea\n       </a>\n       off the Russian coast have been reduced by at least half since the 1990s as a result of overfishing.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">\n        <a href="#cite_note-69">\n         [69]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_issues">\n        Environmental issues\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Pacific_Ocean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Environmental issues">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Marine_pollution" title="Marine pollution">\n        Marine pollution\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Great_Pacific_garbage_patch" title="Great Pacific garbage patch">\n        Great Pacific garbage patch\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Environmental_impact_of_shipping" title="Environmental impact of shipping">\n        Environmental impact of shipping\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Marine_debris_on_Hawaiian_coast.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="324" data-file-width="432" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Marine_debris_on_Hawaiian_coast.jpg/220px-Marine_debris_on_Hawaiian_coast.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Marine_debris_on_Hawaiian_coast.jpg/330px-Marine_debris_on_Hawaiian_coast.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b3/Marine_debris_on_Hawaiian_coast.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Marine_debris_on_Hawaiian_coast.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Marine_debris" title="Marine debris">\n          Marine debris\n         </a>\n         on a\n         <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">\n          Hawaiian\n         </a>\n         coast\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The quantity of small plastic fragments floating in the north-east Pacific Ocean increased a hundredfold between 1972 and 2012.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">\n        <a href="#cite_note-70">\n         [70]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Marine pollution is a generic term for the harmful entry into the ocean of chemicals or particles. The main culprits are those using the rivers for disposing of their waste.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-news.nationalgeographic.com_71-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-news.nationalgeographic.com-71">\n         [71]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The rivers then empty into the ocean, often also bringing chemicals used as\n       <a href="/wiki/Fertilizer" title="Fertilizer">\n        fertilizers\n       </a>\n       in agriculture. The excess of oxygen-depleting chemicals in the water leads to\n       <a href="/wiki/Hypoxia_(environmental)" title="Hypoxia (environmental)">\n        hypoxia\n       </a>\n       and the creation of a\n       <a href="/wiki/Dead_zone_(ecology)" title="Dead zone (ecology)">\n        dead zone\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">\n        <a href="#cite_note-72">\n         [72]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Marine_debris" title="Marine debris">\n        Marine debris\n       </a>\n       , also known as marine litter, is human-created waste that has ended up floating in a lake, sea, ocean, or waterway. Oceanic debris tends to accumulate at the center of gyres and coastlines, frequently washing aground where it is known as beach litter.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-news.nationalgeographic.com_71-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-news.nationalgeographic.com-71">\n         [71]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In addition, the Pacific Ocean has served as the crash site of satellites, including\n       <a href="/wiki/Mars_96" title="Mars 96">\n        Mars 96\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Fobos-Grunt" title="Fobos-Grunt">\n        Fobos-Grunt\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Upper_Atmosphere_Research_Satellite" title="Upper Atmosphere Research Satellite">\n        Upper Atmosphere Research Satellite\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Major_ports_and_harbors">\n        Major ports and harbors\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Pacific_Ocean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Major ports and harbors">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_ports_and_harbors_of_the_Pacific_Ocean" title="List of ports and harbors of the Pacific Ocean">\n        List of ports and harbors of the Pacific Ocean\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">\n        See also\n       </span>\n       <span
